    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_9682382').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_9682382').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_9682382').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {

  <span id="freeText11370872953249016124" style="display:none">The Ugly Truth (Diary of a Wimpy Kid, #5), Jeff Kinney <br /><br />The story begins with Greg explaining that since he and his best friend Rowley have had a big fight, their friendship has been "history.". <br /><br />Susan Heffley, Greg's mother, announces that she will be going back to college for a few months in order to stimulate her mind. <br /><br />As a result, the Heffley men must take care of themselves, and most stability falls apart. <div id="review_141479506" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/141479506" />
    <a title="Madigan Mirza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3898373-madigan-mirza"><img alt="Madigan Mirza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536772829p2/3898373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/141479506?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madigan Mirza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madigan Mirza" href="/user/show/3898373-madigan-mirza">Madigan Mirza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer141479506" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4977696031920001000">This was a very funny book, but perhaps not quite as funny as the rest of the series. Don't get me wrong! The Ugly Truth has plenty of laugh-out-loud moments. But, while the first four books had me roaring with laughter, erupting in guffaws, and frequently demanding to read aloud portions of the inspired insanity to anyone within earshot while gasping and trying to catch my breath, this latest offering only had me chuckling ruefully, or perhaps breaking out in a broad grin from time to time. I t</span>
  <span id="freeText4977696031920001000" style="display:none">This was a very funny book, but perhaps not quite as funny as the rest of the series. Don't get me wrong! The Ugly Truth has plenty of laugh-out-loud moments. But, while the first four books had me roaring with laughter, erupting in guffaws, and frequently demanding to read aloud portions of the inspired insanity to anyone within earshot while gasping and trying to catch my breath, this latest offering only had me chuckling ruefully, or perhaps breaking out in a broad grin from time to time. I think part of the reason why this book didn't tickle my funnybone as much is because Greg Heffley is growing up. He's always been conscious of being a middle-school boy and a bit of late-bloomer, but this volume has him much more worried about when he's going to catch up with a lot of the guys in his class. There's less random hilarity in this volume, and more of a connected storyline, as Greg ruminates on his still strained friendship with Rowley, his uncle's upcoming wedding, his health class and school slumber party. Greg's obsession with getting more popular, and winning over girls in particular, continues to be charming. <br /><br />I was surprised however, by how much he really didn't get it, in terms of Rowley. Greg has been a selfish friend over the years, but he doesn't see that at all. He just wants things to go back to the way they were, when Rowley put up with all of his abuse. Greg's bored demeanor with everything having to do with his family, and his disappointment at being treated like a little kid at his uncle's wedding (he was hoping to be a full-fledged groomsman, rather than an assistant flower boy) was pretty silly, and the highlight of the book, for me, was the school sponsored sleepover. Convinced he's going to be able to mingle with cute girls all evening, Greg eagerly signs up, but is sorely disappointed when it's mostly guys and their over-earnest teachers take away all of the kids cell phones and electronic devices when they refuse to socialize with each other. Predictably, the helicopter parents arrive to pick up their kids early, fearing the worst when they don't answer their text messages.<br /><br />The blend of humor, and stick figure-like cartoons which convey so much emotion which are the hallmarks of this series are still here and Wimpy Kid fans won't be disappointed in this latest addition.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4977696031920001000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4383802537283597689">You just can't get enough of it.<br/><br/>I have been introduced to these lately and I find it surprisingly addictive. This one brought in little surprises of Greg's mom leaving the house to the men and the resulting dilapidation of the daily routines, the short and thankful introduction of the domestic help and her witty circumventions around the works.<br/><br/>I guess the reason we all find this so intriguing and compelling is that there's that kid inside each one of us. The stupid beliefs that we all had about </span>
  <span id="freeText4383802537283597689" style="display:none">You just can't get enough of it.<br /><br />I have been introduced to these lately and I find it surprisingly addictive. This one brought in little surprises of Greg's mom leaving the house to the men and the resulting dilapidation of the daily routines, the short and thankful introduction of the domestic help and her witty circumventions around the works.<br /><br />I guess the reason we all find this so intriguing and compelling is that there's that kid inside each one of us. The stupid beliefs that we all had about the workings of the universe. Things that we keep to ourselves. Those troll incidents that we want to laugh out loud to but do not want to be associated to our adult images.<br /><br />This book brought many such incidents and packed them into one for me. You might think that you maybe a Tony Stark or something but you sure had some funny mishaps in the world of adults.<br /><br />Or as we call it, 'there's this funny thing that happened to my <i>friend</i> in childhood'.<br /><br />A whooping five star from a 22 year old. :)</span>

<div id="review_278652621" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/278652621" />
    <a title="Prashant" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6303222-prashant"><img alt="Prashant" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/278652621?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Prashant" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Prashant" href="/user/show/6303222-prashant">Prashant</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer278652621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2803373203970788494">I loved this book more than any of the other Wimpy kids for two reasons. First being that it was awesome and funny. Second, this being the last book in my box set I was savoring every page because I knew I have come to the end of the fun journey. I found this book funnier than the others because now Greg has started to have some real issue related to puberty and relations. He is having a tough time dealing and ignoring his one time best friend Rowley and things got worse when Rowley got a pimple</span>
  <span id="freeText2803373203970788494" style="display:none">I loved this book more than any of the other Wimpy kids for two reasons. First being that it was awesome and funny. Second, this being the last book in my box set I was savoring every page because I knew I have come to the end of the fun journey. I found this book funnier than the others because now Greg has started to have some real issue related to puberty and relations. He is having a tough time dealing and ignoring his one time best friend Rowley and things got worse when Rowley got a pimple and started considering himself one among the adults. <br /><br />In this book Greg has to keep on dealing with his problems with Rodrick but not too much space is spent on that. Rather this time the book starts with a lock-out which Greg presumed to be a girl-guys night out and how terribly wrong he turns out to be. The events in this lock-out reminded me of the picnics to the same worn out places my public school used to arrange for us. This time Greg also has to attend one of this uncles fifth wedding and the whole family is going to gather at grammy's house for this event. The description of the family members is legen (wait for it !!) dary :) <br /><br />I just can't contain my smile while writing this review. Can't write anymore because I don't want to take the fun out for the other who are still left to read it. Go for it !! <br />As for me, Cabin Fever is my definite next purchase !!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2803373203970788494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I read almost all the genre but YA, Fantasy, Biographies are the most. My favorite series is, of course, Harry Potter but then there are many more books that I just adore. I have bookcases filled with books which are waiting to be read so can't stay and spend more time in this review, so remember I loved reading this and love reading more, you should also read what you love and then just <a href="https://www.keeponreading.in" rel="nofollow noopener">Keep on Reading</a>.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3137719165794355247"> In this book Greg has lost his best friend Rowley because of an argument that they had.   <span id="freeText3137719165794355247" style="display:none"> In this book Greg has lost his best friend Rowley because of an argument that they had. His best friend Rowley's parents have hired some people to be his friend. Meanwhile Greg Is always bored and has no other friends to do anything with. Everyone out there seems to be having more fun then Greg. He feels left out. Everything is pretty normal at school but Rowley and Greg are trying their best to try to avoid each other. His uncle Gary was having his third wedding which was a complete dag to go to and the entire family had to stay at Gammie's house which he wasn't looking forward to. Gammie's house isn't the most child friendly place and it was also his turn to get "the talk" from Gammie which he wasn't looking forward to. But then something miraculous happened. Jordan Jury one of the most popular kids in the school invited him and Rowley to a huge party. Greg wants to go but his uncle Gary's wedding is on that day so he couldn't go, but Rowley ended up going. Greg finds out that he was going to get a tuxedo, at the wedding only the groomsmen get wear tuxedos. Maybe this going to his uncle's wedding would be a better thing to do instead of going to the party. <br /><br /> From a scale of 1 to 10 I would give this an 8 which goes for every other diary of the wimpy kid book. There were some parts that I really liked but there were some parts that were completely irrelevant to the book. I liked the part about Rowley and him becoming friends. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15965735339295664739">Good Reads<br/><br/>Name: Conner Rodriguez<br/>Book: Diary of a Wimpy Kid: The Ugly Truth<br/>Date: 4/8/13<br/>Period: 4<br/>Author: Jeff Kinney<br/>Summary<br/> I chose the book Diary of a Wimpy Kid because I wanted to continue the series.   <span id="freeText15965735339295664739" style="display:none">Good Reads<br /><br />Name: Conner Rodriguez<br />Book: Diary of a Wimpy Kid: The Ugly Truth<br />Date: 4/8/13<br />Period: 4<br />Author: Jeff Kinney<br />Summary<br /> I chose the book Diary of a Wimpy Kid because I wanted to continue the series. Diary of a Wimpy kid is about two kids named Greg and Rowley who are in there final year in middle school. In their final year there friendship gets a little torn apart by Greg maturing and Rowley still acting like a five year old. My favorite quote in this book is when Greg’s mom makes him fold the clothes and finds his mothers underwear and says “For the record, I think it should be illegal for a boy to have to fold his mother's underwear.” I like this quote because I can relate to this event and how you find your parents underwear, it is totally weird and I get filled with disgust. Diary of a Wimpy Kid is written in third person and Jeff Kinney’s point is to tell the life an unpopular kid in middle school who tries to be the coolest in school. Yes, I would recommend this book to someone. Not just anyone thought, I would only recommend it to young fifth graders who would like to know the life of a middle school student.<br /></span>

<div id="review_133927070" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/133927070" />
    <a title="Reese" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4332751-reese"><img alt="Reese" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1289182586p2/4332751.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/133927070?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reese" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reese" href="/user/show/4332751-reese">Reese</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer133927070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15249912264572852420"> Diary of a Wimpy Kid: The Ugly Truth<br/> Life Can Be Hard Sometimes<br/>	What would you do if the weekend before going back to school you broke up with your best friend... maybe your only friend at all. In The Ugly Truth, an auto-biography by Jeff Kinney, takes place in a bunch of settings, like Gregory's house, and his school. It's the beginning of the year and Greg got in another fight with his best friend Rowley, and they are no longer talking anymore, and to make matters even more awkward Rowleys be</span>
  <span id="freeText15249912264572852420" style="display:none"> Diary of a Wimpy Kid: The Ugly Truth<br /> Life Can Be Hard Sometimes<br />	What would you do if the weekend before going back to school you broke up with your best friend... maybe your only friend at all. In The Ugly Truth, an auto-biography by Jeff Kinney, takes place in a bunch of settings, like Gregory's house, and his school. It's the beginning of the year and Greg got in another fight with his best friend Rowley, and they are no longer talking anymore, and to make matters even more awkward Rowleys been hanging out with college age kids that Greg thinks are being hired from a company called “Cool Brian” by Rowley's parents. This all stinks because Greg is of the age where people in his grade start going to parties and kid's parents expect them to have more of a responsibility for themselves. This is really ruff because Gregory has to experience all these big changes, without his ex-best friend, Rowley. I rated Jeff Kinney's novel The Ugly Truth, five out of five stars because It was very humorous, and had some parts that were really realistic to the life of a middle school student. Times become confusing for Greg when he has to make new friends, has to take more responsibility for his actions, and has to face the ugly facts about being a teenager.<br />	Times became confusing for Greg when he had to make new friends in the beginning of the school year, because he had just recently broken up with his best friend Rowley, who he had been a jerk too. “I'm actually starting to get a little concerned, because school starts back up in a few days, and if we're going to get this friendship back on track, something needs to happen quick.” (1.) So finally, Rowley decided to stand up for himself and hang out with other people, actually hired college students... but thats okay.<br />	Additionally, Times become confusing for Greg, when he has to take more responsibility for his actions. This year, teachers are expecting more from all the students, and parents are expecting more from their kids. “Ms. Grove hired me to take care of her plants while she was on a business trip. I did it for the first few days, and then I guess you could say I got busy with other things [...] She was mad about her plants, too, because unfortunately most of them didn't make it. [...]Ms. Grove said she wouldn't hire me again even if her life depended on it. Then she sent me home without paying.” (74.)Greg also discovers he has to take more responsibility for his actions because he realizes he's been a real jerk to his friends and family lately, and know it's to late for him to change things because his friend already ditched him. <br />	Finally, times become confusing for Greg, when he has to face the ugly truth about being a teenager. When your in middle school things can get very difficult, like new math homework your parents just don't get. “ It's been a long time since dad was in school, so I have to sit there and wait while he reads my textbook and gets caught up.” (64.) Also, you must face big parties, and friendship issues.<br />	In contrast, times become confusing for Greg when he has to make new friends, has to take more responsibility for his actions, and has to face the ugly facts about being a teenager. I actually have a few connections to the novel The Ugly Truth , when Greg was invited to a big party it reminded me of all the Bar and Bat Mitzvah I've been to last year. As most people know, they are usually the biggest parties people attend to in seventh grade. I remember I was really nervous going to my first one, but then I found it to be really fun. Also, I can relate to Greg when he said his dad needed to catch up on the math, because when my dad helps me with math, he usually has to look back in the book to see how to do different kinds of new math skills we do in school these days. From reading this book I've learned that you should treat other people the way you want to be treated, because Greg was a bad friend to Rowley and when Rowley left him, Greg had a hard time making new ones because of his some what unbecoming behavior.<br />	In conclusion, I think I did well on this essay. I actually had to read this book in a short period of time because I lost my novel I was reading before this, and I've spent about five hours all together typing, and filling out my outline. I thought highlighting all the words we're easy, but typing the whole thing was more difficult. If I had more time on this assignment, I would definitely read a more challenging book, but due to the short time I had after loosing my book and between the due date of this book review, I had to read something quickly! For the next review I will make sure I do not lose my book.</span>

<div id="review_340330291" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/340330291" />
    <a title="Xander Graham" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6362141-xander-graham"><img alt="Xander Graham" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319411230p2/6362141.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/340330291?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Xander Graham" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Xander Graham" href="/user/show/6362141-xander-graham">Xander Graham</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer340330291" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8844312411593716440">Diary of a Wimpy Kid the Ugly Truth<br/>by Jeff Kinney<br/>published 2010<br/>fiction<br/><br/>	Greg, the protagonist, writes in a diary most everyday. The setting is everywhere around Greg's house and the school that he goes to. There is no main problem in this book but some are Greg and his friend Rowley trying to become friends again after a long time of not talking to each other. Another problem that was in the book was when he tried to get into a commercial but failed to another kid that wasn't as good as him. The </span>
  <span id="freeText8844312411593716440" style="display:none">Diary of a Wimpy Kid the Ugly Truth<br />by Jeff Kinney<br />published 2010<br />fiction<br /><br />	Greg, the protagonist, writes in a diary most everyday. The setting is everywhere around Greg's house and the school that he goes to. There is no main problem in this book but some are Greg and his friend Rowley trying to become friends again after a long time of not talking to each other. Another problem that was in the book was when he tried to get into a commercial but failed to another kid that wasn't as good as him. The title of the book relates to the end of the story. When he finds out information from his grandma that he did not want to find out but was worried about it throughout the story.<br />	The theme of the book would be about how instead of putting too much thought into something before it happens know what the chances are of whatever it is really happening. An example of this is when Greg wants to get into the commercial and putts so much thought into it before he even knew if he can go to see if he could be in the commercial. Another example was when he spent the night at his school and it ended up with a lot more rules than he thought. One last example was when he was thinking of what his grandma will say to him and always avoiding her even though it could have not been too bad.<br />	I would recommend this to my friends because it is a very easy and fun read that people in middle school can relate too in some areas. For example I understood what Greg was going through with his family a lot of the time. Compared to other books I have read i would say that the book was short and fun but I don't ever think that the series would ever go into as much details like the hunger games would.<br />	A quote from the book could be from page 123 when Greg sends letters to his maid that never really did her job and Greg was trying to change that by sending her notes that he said was from his mom. But the maid always gave excuses for doing her job and the only reason the house was clean at the end of the day is because the Greg's mom made everyone clean up before the maid came even though she would have to clean the house.<br />	The book made me realize that i shouldn't think too much about things that might happen in the future but instead I should think about the things that could make me get to the thing that I originally wanted. This book also made me realize that I shouldn't think that something will be bad but instead that it will be good. If it is bad then you deal with it.<br /><br />- Xander Graham</span>
  <a data-text-id="8844312411593716440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SAyFeZ8g1ihRFKdpbeMw8gmSi2ACKbMlg+GFD/fw56JyKuyrJH4fQPY/EwiaFjot381sqMykPULYn8O+OrMVOA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

            if ($('bookCover_30051627').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_30051627').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
